Chun Qiu (Spring and Autumn)

Tidbits 184

— (Xu Shu-ren)

"爭" (zhēng), "to compete," means to vie for, to invade. "掙" (zhèng), "to struggle," means to strive for liberation. The former is the action of the strong, the latter is the manifestation of the weak's resistance. However, "爭" is a habit that the strong are unwilling to give up even on their deathbeds. "掙" is not necessarily something that everyone can use—because there are many weak people who, when they see the strong coming to annex them, give in at once!

If the strong abandon "爭," the world will immediately be at peace. If the weak abandon "掙," not only will there be no peace, but it will only promote the growth of war! Facts tell us: "'爭' will not disappear." Then the group of the weak should march in unison, unite their front, and desperately "掙"! While there is still breath, this ambition must not be relaxed even slightly. Even if they perish from struggling, it is glorious, and there are many more weak people who continue to struggle!

Brutal strong people! You must not take "爭" as the precious raft to prolong your life. You must know that the weak will awaken fiercely. They will awaken that "掙" is the only tool for them to preserve their lives! They want to realize their hopes under "掙." Beware! The result of that kind of "爭" cannot resist this "掙"!

In a Certain Coffee Shop 185

— Hua Ling

Following my friend, I came out of the cinema and strolled into a nearby coffee shop. A waitress, only eighteen or nineteen years old, with a round face, although not beautiful, but not repulsive, skillfully greeted us and seated us. From the corners of her mouth, which were covered with thick powder and rouge, a shallow dimple emerged, and she gently placed a small notepad with a pencil attached in front of my friend. From her crimson lips, a sentence flowed out, "You haven't been here for a week."

"That's right," my friend nodded, then said, "Two coffees with milk. If you're free, get yourself one too." The waitress nodded, twisted her waist, and went to the back room. Before long, she brought three cups of steaming milk, placed them on the small round table, and sat down next to my friend. While stirring the milk, she quietly asked my friend, "Is that short-lived Xiao Lu still in Shanghai?" My friend shook her head and said, "Forget it, do you still need to be so serious with him?" The waitress lowered her eyes and said firmly, "One day, when I find him, I will definitely settle the accounts of this past year with him."

"Alright, everything will be on my account," my friend said with a playful smile, breaking the depressing atmosphere. I couldn't help but laugh, which made the waitress laugh too. While laughing, she glared at my friend, but my friend pretended not to see it and solemnly repeated, "Everything will be on my account, alright."

Under the soft dark green light, we sat for nearly forty minutes, listening to the waitress recount her romance with Xiao Lu. In a scene filled with two bags of tears and gritted teeth, my friend left two dollars, put on her hat, and pulled me out of the coffee shop. On the dusk-lit street, she took a deep breath, tossed away a rubber-tipped cigarette butt, and said, "Old brother, are you interested in settling this karmic debt for Xiao Lu?"

"I obey your command, but I don't know if it will be on your account?" I said, and we both laughed at each other.

In a sound of good night, I went home with staggered steps. But from that day on, I don't know why, I seemed to have one more worry.

The Cow Nose Go to the Front Lines! 186

The Standard Husband 187

— Wei Jing

The "Standard Husband" is a new neighbor of mine, a title respectfully bestowed upon him by several ladies in our shikumen neighborhood.

Speaking of this Standard Husband, he truly lives up to the name. He works in a foreign firm, is around thirty-five years old, has no children, and no maids. The entire household consists of just him and his wife. His wife is a large woman, weighing at least one hundred and sixty pounds. The couple's love is extremely deep.

This Standard Husband always gets up at dawn. The first things he does after getting up are wiping the windows, sweeping the floor, and washing the teacups. After finishing these tasks, he goes to buy groceries with a basket. Generally, before eight o'clock, he returns home with a basket of groceries. At the same time, he always buys some breakfast to bring back. He eats half of the breakfast and leaves the other half for his wife. After eating breakfast, he busies himself with scaling fish or cutting meat, followed by washing vegetables and rinsing rice. If the weather is clear, he even has to steal a moment to hang several bamboo poles of clothes to dry. It's not until eight forty-five that he puts on his hat and goes to work.

His wife, regardless of the weather, always gets up at ten o'clock. After washing up and having a light breakfast, she goes downstairs to cook rice. By the time it's a quarter past twelve, the rice is cooked, and the husband returns. Then, she goes back to her room to rest, and her husband prepares the dishes. Bringing the food upstairs, serving the rice, washing the bowls, and other tasks are all the Standard Husband's job. After lunch, the Standard Husband takes care of things briefly and then goes back to work. His wife goes downstairs to play mahjong. (If there's no mahjong game, she closes the door and takes a nap.) Needless to say, the serving of dinner is also the Standard Husband's responsibility.

Saturday afternoon is the Standard Husband's floor-washing day. In two hours, he can scrub and wash the floor spotlessly clean.

This Standard Husband resolutely shoulders all the heavy household responsibilities himself, truly making him one of a kind. Except for emptying the chamber pot and washing clothes, which are handled by a maid from another family, he does everything himself. His wife simply sleeps and plays mahjong every day, living a very carefree life. Therefore, several ladies in the neighborhood all feel a sense of regret at not having met him before getting married, and they envy the Standard Husband's wife for having such great fortune.

However, people are always unsatisfied. In the ladies' casual conversations, she always reveals that her husband also has his shortcomings. Although he is willing to do things, he just doesn't earn a lot of money.

Notes on What I Saw 188

— (Lan Shan)

The other morning, around seven o'clock, a police van that also catches beggars stopped at the intersection of North Jiangxi Road and Old Race Course Road. Several Chinese and foreign detectives got out of the car and entered several private brothels that specialize in catering to foreign soldiers, to arrest people. These prostitutes were just in the middle of their sweet dreams when they were grabbed from their beds, their hair disheveled, their faces lonely, their clothes unkempt, and their eyes drowsy. When they saw the police officers, who looked like wolves and tigers, they were scared out of their wits. Some, with little courage, cried tears profusely. Some, with enough guts, looked for an opportunity to run away. But in the end, it was like catching turtles in a jar, easily done. In less than half an hour, they had already "loaded a car full." At that time, the author was moved by the scene and wrote a poem lamenting: "Seven o'clock in the morning, the police van arrives; inside Gengfu Lane, chickens fly everywhere in chaos."

It is said that after they are arrested, they are transferred from the police station to the court. If it is proven that they do not wish to pursue this carnal life, they can be sent to charitable organizations to live. If they voluntarily engage in prostitution, they are fined and released according to the situation. But strangely, none of them were forced into prostitution; ninety-nine percent said they were willing. Because they know that charitable organizations are not as good as brothels in terms of clothing, entertainment, and food.

After they are released, they will soon be arrested and fined again. -- It is said that they will be fined until they are afraid and change their profession. -- What a good solution! Excellent!

Swapped Phoenixes 189

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Three: Gentle Rain and Slanting Wind Leave Traces; Deep Night, Silent Person Writes a Letter of Severance

Old Mrs. Zhang said: This is about today. These past few days, I've seen you sitting in your study, just sitting and brooding, and I don't know what's wrong. Guoqi smiled: You are just too loving of your son, thinking too much about everything; there's really nothing. Old Mrs. Zhang said: As long as there's nothing wrong with you, that's good. Would I want you to have something on your mind? After dinner, Guoqi didn't dare go out again and stayed in his study to read. However, after reading three or five pages, he started daydreaming again. His mother's question today was not without reason. He's been making good progress these past few days. Yesterday, during their last meeting, when he was holding his hat, the other person looked at him and even nodded in acknowledgement. If this continues, he can talk to him. Originally, they've known each other to this extent, yet he still doesn't know the other person's name. That's really not right. He must speak to him every time he sees him from now on. What should he say as the first sentence? I'll start according to Western customs: "Miss, may I ask your surname?" But what if he doesn't agree? Or simply won't? Because they've known each other for about a month, he already knows that I'm Zhang Litian. He has seen him holding magazines several times, and those magazines all contain my writing. On this point, it proves that they are literary acquaintances. If we're literary acquaintances, why can't we exchange names? He is willing to read my writing, so he definitely won't refuse my question. I'll take a risk. What's there to be afraid of? In any case, he can't ignore me. Thinking to this point, it's as if a difficult math problem has been solved, and he reaches out to slap the table. But after the sound, he immediately realizes that this noise shouldn't be heard by his mother. He immediately calms down and looks at a book in front of him. Fortunately, his mother didn't hear the noise, and it passed without incident. The next day, when he woke up, it was already drizzling. The alleys were muddy, as if it had been raining all night. In this kind of weather, the young ladies probably wouldn't be willing to get wet going to school. Even if they do go to school, they'll take a car, how could they walk? It would be pointless to take a detour today to meet him. He could also not go at all. But in order to maintain his own faithfulness, even if he doesn't meet him, he must take this detour, so that if he still comes to school, he won't miss him. With this thought, Guoqi went out with an umbrella in the rain, walking slowly, looking around in those narrow alleys. But after he had walked through all those narrow alleys, the rain was falling diagonally like a net of threads. He suddenly smiled to himself. This is really too faithful of me. If I were a female student, I wouldn't come out in such heavy rain. Thinking to himself, a gust of wind came, and the umbrella couldn't hold on, splashing his face with rain. He started walking faster, about to go to school. Unexpectedly, at the turn in the road, under the gate of a large house, there was already a small umbrella extending from under the eaves. (39)

Local Customs Small Records

The Dark Side of Japanese Tourist Guides 190

— Ji Yun

Visiting the three islands of Japan is just a matter of seeing a few shrines and a few hot springs. But with effective publicity and tall tales, naturally Westerners come from thousands of miles away to sightsee and experience Eastern flavors. The profits from tourism in the spring and autumn seasons are very prosperous, so the special agencies of the Japan Tourism Bureau are permanently thriving. Westerners who visit Japan must hire guides, whom the Japanese call "案内" (annai). This special profession is mostly filled by hotel waiters and rickshaw pullers, with about two hundred people nationwide. There are many dark secrets involved, such as taking foreigners to prostitutes or cheating them out of money when buying antiques. Chinese who come to Japan for sightseeing are mostly led by students studying abroad and do not need "annai." Moreover, they can't fool the Chinese with a few Chinese characters, so they don't like guiding Chinese people.

There is an "Annai" association in Yokohama, where each member has to contribute two or three thousand yuan of capital. There are no vacancies, which shows that this profession is very lucrative. They accompany tourists in turn according to their numbers, but tourists can also specify who they want to hire. Their daily income is about seven to ten yuan, but tourist ships only come and go for about four months a year. The rest of the time, they have to do other business or live off their savings. Therefore, most of them also deal in antiques, and their wives open unique secret hotels in Yokohama.

Guides spend the whole day with foreigners, eating Western food and riding in cars, living a very comfortable life. Even if they stay in a three-yuan room in a hotel, they can earn one yuan back. So, all hotels that cater to tourists are in cahoots with them, otherwise, even the Imperial Hotel would have to close down. Not to mention hotels, they also have secret commissions on other purchases and geishas playing the shamisen. Moreover, foreigners who come to Japan for sightseeing are all rich, and a few thousand yuan is not a big deal. Once, an American woman bought an earthenware pot for thirty yuan in a village in Nikko, and the guide got one-third of the money. Another time, an American tycoon saw an ancient Buddha in an antique store in Yokohama, but the deal didn't go through. The guide spoke eloquently, insisting that it was from the Kamakura period and that there were only three in all of Japan, except for Yokohama, Kyoto, and Nikko. Later, he led him to an antique store in Nikko, where they found the same statue, with even better gold plating than the one in Yokohama. He bought it for six thousand yuan. In fact, the ancient Buddha in Yokohama had already taken the train to Nikko at the request of the guide, waiting for him there. Japanese antiques often circulate in Kobe and Nagasaki, all waiting for tourists to come.

Thirty years ago, the geisha Yuki-musume of Gion in Kyoto became Mrs. Malga once and earned tens of thousands of yuan. There are even more prostitutes, courtesans, and geishas in Tokyo who have made fortunes by gaining the favor of foreigners. Girls from the countryside are often introduced by guides to be temporary partners of tourists. As long as there is money, they can be bought and sold at a price. This may be why foreigners are so fond of Japan. There are also those who become foreign women's gigolos through guides, such as Matsumoto, who traveled around Japan with an Italian middle-aged woman for three months, like a couple. After they parted, he used his savings to open a furniture store in Yokohama. There was also an old woman from New Gold Mountain who died of illness while sightseeing in Japan and gave all her savings in the Yokohama Specie Bank to the guide, instructing him to transport her bones back to her hometown, which was an unexpected windfall.

There are also a dozen female guides, who have lived in France or the United States for many years and speak fluent foreign languages. They also have considerable experience in socializing and cohabiting with foreigners. They wear gorgeous clothes and are more modern than dance girls. In the hotels of Hakone, Nikko, and Atami, they accompany tourists in and out. Who would recognize them as Japanese? Recently, the Tourism Bureau has been considering using female guides, but that is another matter. (Translated from "Talk" magazine, April issue, page 323)

Page 17

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Song of Moods 191

— Liang Qiyun

I was raised with this kind of education from a young age. — When I was little, if I ever mixed with the cowherds or the children of the tenant farmers to play, my grandmother would forcefully drag me home and say to me in a stern and threatening tone, "I've told you a thousand times, ten thousand times, to not mix with them, but you just won't listen. When you grow up, I'll make you a farmer who steps in cow dung and mud."

Then, in my free time or before going to bed, I would clamor for stories. My grandmother often painted pictures of the luxurious lives of people like Uncle Yongquan and Second Master Dingxiang (the big landlords in my hometown).

In my young heart, these left a slight impression that persists to this day:

...Holding a dry tobacco pipe, dressed neatly, strolling leisurely and comfortably on the embankment. As soon as the tenant farmers saw them, they would rush forward to greet them and ask how they were doing. And they had huge rice granaries at home, several wives, and were creditors to many families in the village...

And I myself, without knowing why, gradually envied this kind of life. Towards those who struggled in the vortex of life, especially the boatmen who pulled ropes, the farmers who plowed and planted rice, and the rickshaw pullers, I had a sense of contempt and disdain. As for why I did this, I didn't have a good reason to explain it clearly.

Later, I learned some new and pretty words, and for those people who, in a disguised form, used their labor for food, I called them "slaves of life"!

I had a cousin who got a bachelor's degree from the University of Hong Kong. Once, when I met him in Shanghai, I heard him often use "lowly, despicable things" as a curse. I also imitated him, and whenever those so-called slaves of life angered me, I would curse, "Lowly, despicable things."

My grandmother and uncles all praised me for "having backbone" and "making progress."

Time increased my age.

It's really strange; I don't know when I caught a difficult-to-cure disease. When I was alone, thinking or reading something, my heart would become troubled. It was as if, in a gloomy sky, the surrounding black clouds were all gathered in one place. At the same time, it was as if my heart had become a stubborn stone, unable to be broken with a knife or chopped with an axe.

Every year at the end of the year or during festivals, I would see my father stomp home, sighing towards the dark sky, even turning green in the face and collapsing in a chair... and,

Year after year, I always received too many unsatisfactory events. I watched hope vanish one by one like bubbles. I was depressed, frustrated, and resentful. Fate was like a devil to me, cunning, sly, and very cruel. I was angry! - Although those unsatisfactory things were caused by too many dreams! During the day, I cursed it; (bad luck, bad luck that made my family decline day by day). I cursed it at night too. But the more I did this, the devil seemed to stalk me like a ghost. Before I knew it, it would invade my body again. I tried again and again to get rid of the devil, but it wasn't that simple. Bad luck always hindered the arrival of good dreams and mercilessly occupied me entirely, whether in spring, summer, or autumn...

In this way, I couldn't help but feel troubled and terrified about everything. — A universal feeling of trouble and terror towards every tiny thing.

I felt that my mood had changed.

I was now tired of the things I had previously envied, hating them as if I were smelling a rotten odor on them. Towards the so-called slaves of life that I had previously despised, I instead increased a sense of sympathy.

Whenever I looked in the mirror, gently stroking my haggard cheeks, I couldn't help but sigh. -

"Tomorrow, ah, tomorrow, what kind of day will it be"!

Shopkeeper Guo 192

— Zou Heng

Shopkeeper Guo's shop hadn't had business for a long time. Although buyers still kept coming in every day, most of them just asked about the price and walked out with a cold laugh, without looking back. One day, two days, one month, two months, it was always like this, and Shopkeeper Guo couldn't stand it anymore. He gritted his teeth and said to the shop assistant,

"Let's go for it, lower the price again!"

"But, Shopkeeper Guo, we're not even making a penny of profit on our goods anymore. The coarse goods are already discounted by 5%, doing this is simply..." The shop assistant and accountant, Wang Dali, said to him, but later, seeing Shopkeeper Guo's pale face, he didn't have the courage to continue. In fact, Shopkeeper Guo understood all of this in his heart. He knew that the price of his shop's goods couldn't be lowered anymore. Even selling them at this price was at a loss. But rather than leaving them on the shelves, it was better to sell them at a loss.

"Lower it again, discount it by 20% off the original price!" he said to the shop assistant, his face even paler and his teeth clenched even tighter. This time, Wang Dali didn't say anything, just stared at Shopkeeper Guo's bloodless face. He knew that what the shopkeeper was doing was simply ruining himself. But what could he do? Other shops were mostly selling untaxed goods, and their costs were half as much as his. If he didn't lower the price again, he would only be able to keep them on the shelves forever. He knew the shopkeeper's difficulties, and he also knew that even like this, he couldn't compete with other shops. But! But, he stopped thinking. In the distance, there was endless darkness.

"Let's take a chance"! His final conclusion.

That night, they worked all night, re-pricing the goods. The next morning, as soon as it was light, Wang Dali put up the written colored-paper low-price advertisements, "Selling at a loss, low-price liquidation!" Shopkeeper Guo paced back and forth outside the counter, sometimes looking outside the door. A truck carrying goods of various kinds was passing in front of them, and two XX people were following behind the truck, driving straight to the gate of the Tiantai shop diagonally opposite.

"Smuggled goods"! It was like two bombs exploding in front of his eyes. He took a step back unconsciously, leaning on the counter inside the door.

"What's wrong"? Wang Dali dropped the goods he was sorting and ran over to support him. He shook his hand, indicating that he was fine, while struggling to sit up. In his heart, he clearly realized that his shop was "finished"!

"Ten years of hard work ah"! He gently spat out these words.

"Shopkeeper Guo," Wang Dali walked to his side and said in a low voice. "Things have already come to this, there's no use being sad. Who could have expected the foreign smuggled goods to come so fiercely? But it's not just our shop that's affected in the market: Hongsheng, Yuanli, Yongfengtai, which one isn't like this? Of course, their owners are strong and still have a good reputation in the market, but small shops like ours can't stand it. But," he lowered his voice even more, pointing at the shop diagonally opposite the door, "why don't we do the same? There are several foreign firms in Tianjin. As long as you pay half in cash and find a shop guarantor, you can pick up the goods. There are still two hundred yuan in cash in the till now. Don't pay the rent for this month first. The loan from Yonghe Bank has already been delayed for two months. If you talk nicely and add the interest for this month, and postpone the repayment of the principal for another month, you can use this cash to buy a batch of goods from Tianjin, as long as..." Before he could finish speaking, he was interrupted by Shopkeeper Guo.

"I've thought about this too. It's easy to deal with the landlord, but Yonghe Bank is probably not easy to pester, but we have no choice but to do this. Let's take a chance"! The matter was decided like this. Wang Dali took all the cash and went to Tianjin by car. Shopkeeper Guo stayed alone in the shop. He rewrote the advertisement to "Half-price liquidation!"

Sure enough, there were more buyers, and Shopkeeper Guo was busy alone. Watching the goods on the shelves decrease day by day, he felt an unspeakable ease in his heart, but this ease was also mixed with bitter juice.

One day, two days, three days, Wang Dali hadn't returned yet, and Shopkeeper Guo became anxious. He suspected that he had run away with the money. But thinking about it, Wang Dali wouldn't be that kind of person. They had been shop partners for seven years.

In the afternoon, he received news that it was because Wang Dali had ordered too few goods, and the foreigners were unwilling to deliver them. He was caught by customs officers while smuggling them in from the main road.

In the evening, Shopkeeper Guo's shop closed its doors especially early. The next day, it didn't open again. It wasn't until the third day that someone found him hanging straight from the beam.

Yellow Peel (Continued from Yesterday) 193

— Chou Tong

"I'm afraid they're going to build a car road here! They've put up stakes all over the garden and the house!"

Black Bone Two's heart sank as if it had fallen into a pit. His mouth trembled, and he didn't know how to ask: "Car road — um, what are you talking about?"

The son glanced at his father and then said: "Everyone says that those stakes bring misfortune, not good fortune. Huang Debiao from the yamen also told me that they're going to build it. Back then, when they built the car road at the end, they also put up these kinds of stakes first. The land where the stakes are put up will be seized to build the car road, and even the graves will be dug up —"

Black Bone Two groaned, coughing. He coughed until his face was red. He stroked his chest and asked his son, panting:

Page 18

"They'll take it by force?"

"If they don't take it by force, who's going to be friendly with you!" The son said: "If it's really like that... hum, depending on them is not reliable!" He shook his head.

Black Bone Two groaned as if he had been hit by a hammer in the dark. He trembled and said: "Maybe they won't build a car road..."

He wanted to find some comfort from his son's face, but his son's face was so gloomy, like the twilight of the "plum rain season." He couldn't find any comfort at all.

Black Bone Two groaned for a while, turned his eyes towards the door, and cluelessly packed a pipe of tobacco. The dry tobacco flashed red and black in the dark. It was like a light of hope flashing before his eyes.

"I can ask for a high price, so the yamen can't afford it," he calculated a very high price. He wanted to ask for a price that would scare the yamen. "I'll ask for a price of ten thousand strings of cash!"

So he was happy. "Who would be willing to spend ten thousand strings of cash to buy these two old houses and dozens of yellow peel trees?..." Thinking of this, he smiled slightly, forgetting about the road construction and sitting outside the door to smoke, just like he did every evening.

"If you don't have money, you're giving it to the public!" Finally, in the early summer when the yellow peel flowers bloomed, Black Bone Two's hope was shattered by this iron-like voice. Two very wide lines of lime, from south to north, decided his future life and fate.

When they started building the road, Black Bone Two's heart ached like it was being cut. Watching the house and garden that had been passed down from his ancestors, not sold because of his own lack of success, but taken over by the car road... he cried and shouted day and night. He told the passersby. He looked completely like a madman.

Now, the yellow peel is bearing fruit again. In the yellow peel gardens of the nearby houses, each tree is filled with clusters of yellow peel, flashing proud, yet innocent smiles in the evening sunset. A gust of wind swept past, and the branches swayed. Clusters of yellow peel, crowded together, like tens of thousands of people moving in a grand gathering place.

Black Bone Two watched, remembering his former yellow peel garden. - That's right, at this time of year in the past, there could be good income, how could it be like now, with no morning or evening? He held the pipe under his arm, scratched his gray and messy hair, and sighed. He straightened his body.

His eyes were already failing, and the twilight made it worse. Looking at the clusters of yellow peel in front of him, they suddenly turned into countless gold, flowing, shining with a bright light, luring him. At this time, he really wished he could grab it with one hand and hold it in his arms! Even if the gold crushed him to death, he would be willing. However, as soon as his eyes blinked, the countless gold turned back into yellow peel.

Cold Water Bath (1) 194

— Er He

I grew up in the countryside, and as a child, I was extremely fond of cold water baths. It wasn't until I mingled in the city that I learned about swimming. But what's the difference between swimming and cold water baths? Swimming is a fashionable name in the city, while cold water bath is a simple and rustic name in the countryside. Swimming is envied by everyone in the city, and a modern man or woman who doesn't know how to swim is considered unqualified. However, cold water baths in the countryside don't attract much attention from adults. They think it's only something for people who catch fish and crabs. Why would someone who doesn't catch fish and crabs take a cold water bath? Therefore, wealthy children are often prevented by adults from having the opportunity to take cold water baths. But poor children's parents are a bit more lenient with their lives. They also have the opportunity to take cold water baths for convenience in making a living (they can catch fish and crabs in the water in the summer to earn money). However, children's personalities are the same after all. Even wealthy children always yearn for cold water baths. Therefore, the more stubborn and brave ones learn to take cold water baths in this situation. However, adults always say:

"This child, instead of studying and acting like an adult, is soaking in the water all day doing something useless!"

But the children insist on bathing. Isn't this passion probably the same as city dwellers' passion for swimming? When I was a child, I was happiest taking cold water baths. But I was an only child, and my parents often kept me from playing near the ditches. But I would secretly go whenever I had the chance. Because of this, my parents, who loved me very much, would reluctantly hit me a few times, thinking that it would make me a well-behaved child. But I would still sneak to the ditches to watch the other children take cold water baths, trying to figure out their tricks so that I could float and sink as freely as they did.

He Yunfang, He Qinfang's Twin Pearl Ball

Sino-Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "Ode to the Red Cliff"

Romantic scholar in Huangzhou. Every day, he enjoys himself by the river. On the sixteenth day of the ninth month in the renxu year, he meets two or three close friends and talks. They elegantly ascend the Red Cliff boat together. Soon, the moon rises from the eastern mountain. Leaning on the railing, they gaze at the Dipper constellation. They strike the strings and clap the beat, singing of the bright moon. They frequently fill their cups with Li Bai's wine. One song, one drink. The guest harmonizes with the xiao flute, the sound and rhythm are deep. The guest is Yang Daoshi from Western Sichuan, blowing a fluttering sound and a lingering rhythm. It's as if a widow is weeping in a solitary boat. One can sigh at Cao Mengde, who composed poetry and brandished his spear in leisurely pleasure. He defeated Jingzhou and flowed smoothly for a thousand miles. He was indeed a hero of his time. I don't know where he is now. Thirty-six thousand days pass easily. How fortunate is life as a mayfly? One must see through empty fame and fortune. Talking about poverty and success embarrasses me. Wash the cups and drink. Gather the dishes. The scattered cups are not free. They pillow each other on the boat.

Zhang Yuanxue, Zhang Huanyue Story Opening

Lili (1240) 9:05 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening: "Simple Prodigy"

Gusts of west wind blow across the east. Meeting an old fisherman at the bridgehead. He often provides three meals a day. The young scholar is diligently studying. Suddenly, three knocks are heard on the brushwood gate. Torches and lanterns are visible, layer upon layer. The servants and maids have all dispersed. Only the beautiful girl remains. Could it be that classmates have come to tease? Could it be that demons from the mountain have appeared? Miss listens, call husband. Certainly no fleeting love. This slave is not an unknown woman. Her father is called Ma in the court. He coveted wealth and offered the slave to Madam Liang as the Western Palace. The slave is unwilling to follow the traitor. Therefore, I composed a poem on the wall. It was cleverly seen by my father, who was furious. But see the added couplet: "Fame and wealth will come naturally," and the second couplet: "Wealth will eventually turn poor." He dispatched the chief steward to search and capture. He clearly offered me to the young scholar. Jian Sheng listens, his face flushed. He thinks that a thousand pieces of gold are not worth a difficult prison. He thinks that Miss lives in a high hall at home, while the young scholar's walls are collapsing and the roof is leaking. Miss is served by servants and maids at home, while the young scholar is accompanied by a lonely lamp in his room. Miss eats delicacies from land and sea at home, while the young scholar often has empty meals three times a day. Miss wears silk and satin at home, while the young scholar bares his shoulders and chest. He advises the young woman to return home early, so as not to suffer here. Miss listens, with tears in her eyes, waiting to die and return to nothingness, to avoid others gossiping. They are in difficulty when the old fisherman who delivers charcoal in the snow arrives. Act as a matchmaker.

Movie News

Talking with Mr. Chen Chuanlin about Photography 199

— Xin

—Joint Photography Exhibition by Chen and Lu

The second joint photography exhibition by Mr. Chen Chuanlin and Mr. Lu Shifu has begun at Daxin Company on the fourth floor, with hours from 9:00 AM to 7:00 PM.

Regarding the works in this exhibition, I am an amateur in photography art and am not in a position to make any comments. Besides, everyone has different preferences, so the best way is to let photography art enthusiasts see for themselves. As for what is recorded here, it is some conversations about photography that I had with Mr. Chen Chuanlin at the venue.

Among Mr. Chen's works, I think what is commendable is his ode to modern architecture and his regularity of folk life. Although there are also things like "a single oar sound in the landscape" in his works, generally speaking, this tendency is rare.

Every great artist is definitely not giving idlers something to rely on, taking pictures for them to put in the study and living room as decorations. He is standing on the new line of the times, facing the pain of the people, to call for injustice for them. In the current situation where the country is in dire straits, with the patriotic movement in full swing, he should also use his camera to record the real situation. Regarding this point, Mr. Chen said: "Everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the country. We are very willing to do it, but because most of the current photography enthusiasts are amateurs, due to professional constraints, it is difficult to have the opportunity to join in the fun. Even when thinking of going to the countryside to collect some photography materials, it often goes against expectations and is not easy to achieve. Therefore, as it stands, we can only have this wish: to take more photos related to the country and society. As for whether we can do it, that can only depend on whether there is an opportunity."

After that, he led me through their exhibition works, regarding his own works, he cited two works as examples to illustrate how he photographed them.

The first work is number 89 "Deep in the Green Hills," which is a picture taken using top light. He said that usually, we all know that top light is the least suitable light for photography, but there are also exceptions, such as this one, I used top light to take it, because usually, the background behind the mountain always has light, only at noon, the mountain is all black, this thing of mine is to use this opportunity to take.

"Bright Moon Mystery" 200

Nanjing Screen

The second is number 73 photo, is a lot of chickens of different sizes pecking at food very able loving spirit, according to Mr. Chen, when taking this thing, I put a lot of thought into the angle, because if it is taken flat, it will definitely feel very flat visually, and if it is taken from above, the chickens will definitely be very scattered, after considering the results, I used a 45-degree oblique angle to complete it, the result of washing it out, although I dare not say how good it is, but I feel very satisfied with myself.

Later we also talked about some other things, but to save space, I will omit them.

Shen Bao Local Supplement - Automobile Weekly

New Information on the India-Australia "General" Branch Plant 202

— Yu

General Motors of America is one of the largest automobile manufacturers in the world, with huge capital and numerous products. No one denies this. Their headquarters are in the United States, but the cars they manufacture travel all over the world. This is not to mention that, apart from the main factory in the New World, there are quite a few branch factories and shops around the globe. Therefore, it is not meaningless flattery for some people to call them "Universal".

Some of the branch factories set up by General Motors in various places are very large in scale, and the annual turnover is also very considerable. Their goal in setting up branch factories is not only to enable local buyers to obtain lower prices due to the reduction of import taxes and the utilization of local raw materials, but also to employ local workers as much as possible, so that both labor and capital benefit mutually. Now, let's record one of their many factories, General Motors India Limited, and the planned new Australian factory, to get a glimpse.

In India, in recent years, many people feel that there should be an automobile manufacturing company. Although the unfortunate experience of the Calcutta company, this need has not diminished. General (India) Co., Ltd. can be said to be a powerful organization that has emerged in response to this need. The General plant is located in the place of Hughli. They feel very happy to be able to find various talents, workers, etc. in machinery and office work locally. Looking at the numbers below, we can regard this as a powerful proof that is beneficial to India. In the General plant, 97% of the employees are native Indians. In 1935, the company's expenses reached 38,000,000 rupees.

The establishment of factories by General Motors in the local area not only solved the employment problem of Indians, but also brought many benefits to buyers. In the past, a complete car was transported into India fully assembled. The cost of raw materials, labor, and transportation taxes was higher than that of assembling it locally. Therefore, according to General Motors' estimates, the money saved by buyers has reached 12,000,000 rupees.

General Motors' operating statistics for 1935 are as follows:

In order to develop the automobile industry in various places abroad, General Motors often establishes new factories as needed. Recently, General Motors CEO Hanert said, "We firmly believe in Australia's future prosperity and have prepared to build a very large new factory on the banks of the Yarra River in Melbourne." It is said that the area of this new General factory is one of the largest in Australia. The construction of the factory building is expected to be completed in six months, and the number of employees will be approximately 1,500,000. The total cost will reach 400,000 pounds. Hanert has already ordered a large amount of building materials from a steel plant in Australia, and the number of these orders is very large.

The main workshop of the new Australian factory has an area of ​​920 feet by 360 feet, and the total location is 331,200 feet. The material handling machines used in the factory buildings, both overhead and flat types, are widely used. The installation of the testing machine is even more novel. Various road vehicle tests can be carried out on a set of rotating shaft machines. In addition, there is a testing cave with a width of 80 feet, where the final step of testing various vehicles is carried out.

Most of the machines installed in the factory are very new, and some are seen for the first time in Australia. Among them, the car body painting engineering department uses the new principle of air conditioning. After the car body has undergone layer-by-layer painting, it is baked accordingly.

Automobile News Roundup 203

— Yun

American Automobile Production Statistics According to the American "Automobile Daily News", the registration statistics of passenger car production in the spring of this year (except for the numbers of one state and one month that have not been listed) are as follows: In 1936, Chevrolet ranked first with 198,153 vehicles. Ford ranked second with 158,713 vehicles. Plymouth ranked third with 91,393 vehicles. Dodge ranked fourth with 45,360 vehicles. Walter Smobile ranked fifth with 36,653 vehicles. Zeta ranked sixth with 30,360 vehicles. Buick ranked seventh with 27,728 vehicles. Hert Tura Ping ranked eighth with 19,117 vehicles. Stidbeke ranked ninth with 11,965 vehicles. Chrysler ranked tenth with 10,941 vehicles. Paka ranked eleventh with 9,714 vehicles. Nash Rafayette ranked twelfth with 7,553 vehicles. The comparison with the same period in 1935 is Ford 197,757 vehicles. Chevrolet 107,729. Plymouth 83,122. Dodge 36,144. Baotaike 27,002. Walter Smobile 26,807. Hert Tura Ping 14,735. Buick 12,818. Chrysler 8,471. Stidbeke 7,621. Nash Rafayette 5,470. Paka 1,607 vehicles.

Suggestion for Coloring the Speedometer The green, yellow and red lights commonly used in traffic management in major cities around the world are widely used for vehicle traffic safety. It is now proposed to use these three colors on the car speedometer as well. So that drivers can pay attention at any time when the car speed increases. The colored speedometer is green from zero to thirty miles per hour. Yellow from thirty miles to fifty miles per hour. Red above fifty miles. According to the proposer. If the speedometer is divided into these three colors. Then when the needle is pointing from yellow to red. It will inevitably be subject to a spiritual effect and pay attention. The advocate of this proposal is Dr. Stasher of Panlia, Illinois. Qu has a slogan. It is said that "it is best not to point the needle to red."

Women Driving Car Records Mrs. Miller, an American expatriate in Shanghai. He and his daughter drove across America. In six days. Completed the 3,043-mile journey from Washington to Los Angeles. The car she drove was a Plymouth. There were no obstacles except for a punctured tire on the way. The itinerary for the six days is recorded as follows. Depart from Washington at 6:30 AM on the first morning, 407 miles. Bristol at 7:30 AM on the second day, 478 miles. Jackson at 6:30 AM on the third day, 454 miles. Mount Bristol at 6:30 AM on the fourth day, 430 miles. Great Fountain at 6:30 AM on the fifth day, 516 miles. Rosborough at 4:00 AM on the sixth day, 758 miles. The last day of the journey took the longest driving time. It is heard that Mrs. Miller never drove for two consecutive hours. But on that day, she traveled 758 miles in 19 hours. In addition to eating, fueling and resting. An average of forty miles per hour. It is enough to see that women are not incapable of long-term driving.

American Automobile Percentage The United States has always had the largest number of cars in the world. There are three reasons for this. The United States is the largest producer of automobiles. We all know that there are many automobile factories in Detroit. The annual production of cars is in the millions. The production is rich and popular. Automobile prices are lower in the country. Therefore, middle-class families can purchase them. Used as daily transportation products. Not regarded as a luxury item. As for wealthy families, those who own three or four cars are even more common. The number calculated across the country is naturally considerable. The roads in the United States are good. The road lines are very long. And it is the origin of gasoline production, and the driving force and the place of use are superior. I think it is more widely used. According to statistics from the First National Bank of Boston. The current automobile registration statistics in the United States are 24,840,000 vehicles. It actually accounts for 72% of the world's automobile registration.

A Visit to Nissan Motor Co., Ltd. (Continued) 204

— Fang Xijia

Safety Items The entire factory building is constructed with lead-skinned steel bones. Not easy to catch fire. Engine. Generator. The machine wheels are all properly protected. The power generation room is far away from the factory. In order to avoid danger. I heard that since the start of construction. Within three years. There have been no deaths due to work accidents.

Hygiene Items What we can't forget the most in our minds. Is the phenomenon of cleanliness in the factory. There is absolutely no dirt and grease on the factory floor. It's simply so clean that it doesn't look like a factory. Probably the universal love of cleanliness of the Japanese people and the strict management of the factory are the expression. The factory is modeled after the latest type of flat ladder-shaped building. There is ample light. Air circulation. In addition, there is also a large canteen for workers.

Personnel Management The most eye-catching thing. Workers wear uniform uniforms. In good order. They are very diligent and lively at work. There are few signs of fatigue. Workers all stay out. Lunch is only in the factory. Workers have no formal groups or guilds. Only the organizations of the Peace Association and the Sports Association. According to Yun Peace Association is the nature of mutual support for the illness and support for the good fortune of the workers. Anyone who hires a new worker. It must be trained before starting work Yun.

Miscellaneous Remarks 205

The visit lasted for three hours. Only then was it completed. Although I dare not say that the factory is perfect. But with the construction of three years. There is such a great organization. Perfect management. It's really commendable. I can't help but express my great admiration to the people of their country for their efforts in industry. However, if there is no government to make every effort to protect and subsidize and promote. Emerging industries. It is very difficult to make such rapid progress all of a sudden. This shows the enthusiasm of their government for industry. Especially the promotion of heavy military industry. Looking back at the situation in our country. It's really unimaginable.

After that. The reporter once asked the leader. Whether the factory plans to increase the production of large automobiles recently. According to Yun, the local market needs a large number of small automobiles, coupled with the government's special encouragement and promotion for the manufacture of small cars. Such as the special exemption from the driving test regulations. That is, all men and women over the age of sixteen. Allow free driving of small cars. General Exemption from driving tests. Reduce the license tax for small cars and allow no garage regulations. In order to protect the development of the industry. Furthermore, because large cars have fewer sales, the production cost is too high. I am afraid that it will not be able to match the imports from the United States. But when necessary or in wartime. The factory can manufacture large automobiles at any time. In order to replace foreign products and at the same time can be converted into military tanks. Armored car. The possibility of armored trains Yunyun. I hope our authorities and compatriots pay attention to it. (End)

Record of Automobile Accidents in a Week 206

— San Yuan

There were a total of eight automobile accidents in this week. Among them, one man was killed due to serious injuries. Two boys. An Indian. There were three men seriously injured. One man was slightly injured.
